<p>The <b>2006 Winter Olympics</b>, officially known as the <b>XX Olympic Winter Games</b> (French: Les <i>XX<sup>es</sup> Jeux olympiques d'hiver</i>) (Italian: <i>XX Giochi olimpici invernali</i>) and commonly known as <b>Torino 2006</b>, was a winter <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> which was held in <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, from February 10 to 26, 2006. This marked the second time Italy hosted the Olympic Winter Games, the first being the <a href="/wiki/1956_Winter_Olympics" title="1956 Winter Olympics">VII Olympic Winter Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cortina_d%27Ampezzo" title="Cortina d'Ampezzo">Cortina d'Ampezzo</a> in 1956. Italy also hosted the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">Games of the XVII Olympiad</a> in Rome in 1960. Turin was selected as the host city for the 2006 games in June 1999.</p>
<p>The official logo displayed the name "Torino", the Italian name of the city; the city is known as "Turin" in both English and the local traditional language, <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turin_vs._Torino_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turin_vs._Torino-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_mascot" title="Olympic mascot">Olympic mascots</a> of the games were Neve ("snow" in Italian), a female <a href="/wiki/Snowball" title="Snowball">snowball</a>, and Gliz, a male <a href="/wiki/Ice_cube" title="Ice cube">ice cube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mascots_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mascots-5">[5]</a></sup> The official motto of the XX Olympic Winter Games was "Passion lives here".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motto_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Motto-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_city_selection">Host city selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Host city selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PassionLivesHere.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/PassionLivesHere.jpg/220px-PassionLivesHere.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/PassionLivesHere.jpg/330px-PassionLivesHere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/PassionLivesHere.jpg/440px-PassionLivesHere.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PassionLivesHere.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Passion lives here", the Turin 2006 motto written by the Italian calligrapher Francesca Biasetton.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics_bids" title="2006 Winter Olympics bids">2006 Winter Olympics bids</a></div>
<p>Turin was chosen as the host of the Olympics on June 19, 1999, at the 109th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC_Session" title="IOC Session">IOC Session</a> in Seoul, South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bid_archives_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bid_archives-7">[7]</a></sup> This was after the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">IOC</a> had adopted new election procedures during the 108th Extraordinary IOC Session in light of the corruption scandals surrounding the votes for the <a href="/wiki/1998_Winter_Olympics" title="1998 Winter Olympics">1998</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bid_process_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bid_process-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since IOC members were forbidden from visiting the candidate cities (in the interests of reducing bribery), the 109th IOC Session elected a special body, the Selection College, to choose finalist cities from the pool of candidate cities after each had made their final presentations to the full IOC Session.</p>
<p>The full IOC Session then voted on the cities chosen as finalist cities by the Selection College. Although six cities launched candidacies and made presentations to the full IOC Session, the Selection College chose only two cities to go forward to be voted upon by the full IOC Session: <a href="/wiki/Sion,_Switzerland" title="Sion, Switzerland">Sion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bid_archives_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bid_archives-7">[7]</a></sup> The candidacies of <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, Finland; <a href="/wiki/Poprad" title="Poprad">Poprad-Tatry</a>, Slovakia; <a href="/wiki/Zakopane" title="Zakopane">Zakopane</a>, Poland; and <a href="/wiki/Klagenfurt" title="Klagenfurt">Klagenfurt</a>, Austria were dropped by the Selection College after all six candidate cities made their candidate presentations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Election_IOC_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Election_IOC-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The selection of Turin over Sion came as a surprise, since Sion was the overwhelming favorite in part because the IOC is based in Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sion_favorite_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sion_favorite-10">[10]</a></sup> Media speculation was that the choice of Turin was due to the IOC's desire to retaliate against Switzerland for the <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> role played by IOC member <a href="/wiki/Marc_Hodler" title="Marc Hodler">Marc Hodler</a> in the revelation of the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympic_bid_scandal" title="2002 Winter Olympic bid scandal">2002 corruption scandal</a>. Turin's selection came two years after <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>'s unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Bids_for_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Bids for the 2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics bid</a>. Those games were ultimately awarded to Athens, Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whistleblower_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whistleblower-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The information below comes from <a class="external text" href="http://www.aldaver.com/votes.html" rel="nofollow">the International Olympic Committee Vote History</a> web page.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_and_cost_overrun">Cost and cost overrun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cost and cost overrun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>The Oxford Olympics Study</i> established the outturn cost of the Torino 2006 Winter Olympics at USD 4.4 billion in 2015-dollars and cost overrun at 80% in real terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> This includes sports-related costs only, that is, (i) <i>operational costs</i> incurred by the organizing committee for the purpose of staging the Games, e.g., expenditures for technology, transportation, workforce, administration, security, catering, ceremonies, and medical services, and (ii) <i>direct capital costs</i> incurred by the host city and country or private investors to build, e.g., the competition venues, the Olympic village, international broadcast center, and media and press center, which are required to host the Games. Indirect capital costs are <i>not</i> included, such as for road, rail, or airport infrastructure, or for hotel upgrades or other business investment incurred in preparation for the Games but not directly related to staging the Games. The cost and cost overrun for Torino 2006 compares with costs of USD 2.5 billion and a cost overrun of 13% for Vancouver 2010, and costs of USD 21.9 billion and a cost overrun of 289% for Sochi 2014, the latter being the most costly Olympics to date. Average cost for Winter Games since 1960 is USD 3.1 billion, average cost overrun is 142%.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Events_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Events at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Events at the 2006 Winter Olympics</a></div>
<p>The Games featured 84 medal events over 15 disciplines in 7 sports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turin_2006_IOC_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Turin_2006_IOC-1">[1]</a></sup> Events that made their Olympic debut in Turin included mass start biathlon, team sprint cross country skiing, snowboard cross and team pursuit speedskating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Events_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Events-15">[15]</a></sup> The classical men's 50 km and women's 30 km distances, which were held at the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">previous Winter Games</a> in 2002, were not held in these Games, as these events were alternated with freestyle events of the same distances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Most of the cross country skiing events at these Games involved different distances from those in Salt Lake City. The following are the sports and disciplines that were contested at the games. The numbers in parentheses after each sport discipline indicate the number of events contested.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar">Calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chronological_summary_of_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Chronological summary of the 2006 Winter Olympics">Chronological summary of the 2006 Winter Olympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torino_Logo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/Torino_Logo.jpg" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torino_Logo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2006 Olympics logo on display in Turin</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_1_.28Opening_Ceremony.29">Day 1 (Opening Ceremony)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Day 1 (Opening Ceremony)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stefania_Belmondo" title="Stefania Belmondo">Stefania Belmondo</a>, a 10-time Olympic medalist in <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiing</a>, lit the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Flame" title="Olympic Flame">Olympic Flame</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2006 Winter Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> on February 10. Before that, the ceremony celebrated the best of Italy and Sport including a segment honoring the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=FilmMaster_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="FilmMaster Group (page does not exist)">FilmMaster Group</a> K-events (from March 2012: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Filmmaster_Events&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Filmmaster Events (page does not exist)">Filmmaster Events</a>) created and produced the Opening and Closing Ceremonies of the XX Winter Olympic Games in Turin in 2006. Executive Producer <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marco_Balich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marco Balich (page does not exist)">Marco Balich</a>, Content Supervisor <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alfredo_Accatino&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alfredo Accatino (page does not exist)">Alfredo Accatino</a>, Art Direction Lida Castelli. <a href="/wiki/Monica_Maimone" title="Monica Maimone">Monica Maimone</a> of Studio Festi directed the section <i>From Renaissance To Baroque</i>, part of the Opening Ceremony.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_2">Day 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Day 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first gold medal of the 2006 Games was awarded in the 20 kilometre <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Biathlon at the 2006 Winter Olympics">biathlon</a>, won by <a href="/wiki/Germany_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Germany at the 2006 Winter Olympics">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Greis" title="Michael Greis">Michael Greis</a> on the first day of competition. Ice hockey began with the women's competition; <a href="/wiki/Sweden_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Sweden at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Sweden</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Russia at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Russia</a> 3–1 in the first match while <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Canada</a>'s team opened with the second most lopsided win in Olympic history by beating the host <a href="/wiki/Italy_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Italy at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Italians</a> 16–0.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_3">Day 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Day 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 12, <a href="/wiki/Latvia_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Latvia at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Latvia</a> won its first winter Olympic medal when <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81rti%C5%86%C5%A1_Rubenis" title="Mārtiņš Rubenis">Mārtiņš Rubenis</a> took the bronze in the men's luge. <a href="/wiki/Armin_Z%C3%B6ggeler" title="Armin Zöggeler">Armin Zöggeler</a>'s win in that event gave Italy its first gold medal of the Games. Both the Canadian and <a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="United States at the 2006 Winter Olympics">American</a> women's ice hockey teams posted their second straight shutout wins.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_4">Day 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Day 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/China_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="China at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Chinese</a> figure skating pair <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Dan" title="Zhang Dan">Zhang Dan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Hao_(figure_skater)" title="Zhang Hao (figure skater)">Zhang Hao</a>, trailing a dominant <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Russia at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Russian</a> pair, attempted a throw quadruple <a href="/wiki/Salchow_jump" title="Salchow jump">salchow jump</a>—an element which had never been successfully completed in competition. Zhang Dan fell, injuring her knee, but the pair finished their program to a standing ovation and took the silver medal. Russia finished the third day of competition with two gold medals, as did the United States.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_5">Day 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Day 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fourth day saw the two North American women's hockey teams finish out pool play with their third win each. <a href="/wiki/Evgeni_Plushenko" title="Evgeni Plushenko">Evgeni Plushenko</a> of Russia set a world record score in the men's figure skating short program; his 90.66 points was more 10 points better than the nearest opponent's score. The men's combined <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Alpine skiing at the 2006 Winter Olympics">alpine skiing</a> was riddled with disqualifications, including front-runners <a href="/wiki/Bode_Miller" title="Bode Miller">Bode Miller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Raich" title="Benjamin Raich">Benjamin Raich</a>. American <a href="/wiki/Ted_Ligety" title="Ted Ligety">Ted Ligety</a> won the event in what was considered an upset.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_6">Day 6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Day 6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Canada had another strong day on February 15, setting new Olympic records in both men's and women's pursuit team speed skating events as well as opening the men's ice hockey competition with a win against Italy. Italy finished the day with the men's pursuit team Olympic record, however, after the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Netherlands at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Netherlands</a> bettered Canada's time only to have Italy improve upon theirs. China won its first gold of 2006 with <a href="/wiki/Wang_Meng_(speed_skater)" title="Wang Meng (speed skater)">Wang Meng</a>'s victory in the women's individual 500-metre short track speed skating. A pair of <a href="/wiki/Austria_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Austria at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Austrian</a> brothers <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Linger" title="Andreas Linger">Andreas Linger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Linger" title="Wolfgang Linger">Wolfgang Linger</a> won the men's doubles luge while <a href="/wiki/Michaela_Dorfmeister" title="Michaela Dorfmeister">Michaela Dorfmeister</a> gave the nation another championship in the women's downhill.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_7">Day 7</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Day 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kristina_%C5%A0migun" title="Kristina Šmigun">Kristina Šmigun</a> won her second gold medal of the Games with a victory in the women's 10 kilometre classical <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Cross-country skiing at the 2006 Winter Olympics">cross-country skiing</a> on February 16, remaining the only <a href="/wiki/Estonia_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Estonia at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Estonian</a> to medal. In men's <a href="/wiki/Curling_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Curling at the 2006 Winter Olympics">curling</a> action, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Great Britain</a> edged <a href="/wiki/Germany_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Germany at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Germany</a> 7–6, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Switzerland at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Switzerland</a> kept <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="New Zealand at the 2006 Winter Olympics">New Zealand</a> winless by winning 9–7, <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Canada</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Norway</a> 7–6, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="United States at the 2006 Winter Olympics">United States</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Sweden_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Sweden at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Sweden</a>, 10–6. <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> figure skater <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Buttle" title="Jeffrey Buttle">Jeffrey Buttle</a> from <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> won the bronze that year in fact, he is the only non-European man in the top 3 during the men's individual. It was the only medals for him and <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Lambiel" title="Stéphane Lambiel">Stéphane Lambiel</a> from <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_8">Day 8</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Day 8">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 17, <a href="/wiki/Tanja_Frieden" title="Tanja Frieden">Tanja Frieden</a> of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Switzerland at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Switzerland</a> took the gold in women's snowboard cross after <a href="/wiki/Lindsey_Jacobellis" title="Lindsey Jacobellis">Lindsey Jacobellis</a> of the United States fell on the second-to-last jump while performing an unnecessary method grab. Jacobellis settled for silver, while <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Canada</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Maltais" title="Dominique Maltais">Dominique Maltais</a> took bronze after recovering from a crash. <a href="/wiki/Duff_Gibson" title="Duff Gibson">Duff Gibson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Canada</a> took gold in the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Skeleton at the 2006 Winter Olympics">skeleton</a> just ahead of fellow Canadian <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Pain" title="Jeff Pain">Jeff Pain</a>, becoming the oldest individual gold medalist in Winter Olympics history. Rodney Hiner of the United States took home the Bronze. In the women's ice hockey semifinals, the United States lost a shootout to Sweden, marking the first time in international competition that the United States had lost to anyone other than Canada (Canada's win maintained its record of never having lost to anyone other than the United States).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_9">Day 9</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Day 9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kjetil_Andr%C3%A9_Aamodt" title="Kjetil André Aamodt">Kjetil André Aamodt</a> won gold for <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Norway</a> in the men's Super G on February 18, beating <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Maier" title="Hermann Maier">Hermann Maier</a> of <a href="/wiki/Austria_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Austria at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Austria</a>. <a href="/wiki/Germany_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Germany at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Germans</a> <a href="/wiki/Kati_Wilhelm" title="Kati Wilhelm">Kati Wilhelm</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martina_Glagow" title="Martina Glagow">Martina Glagow</a> finished first and second in the 10 kilometre biathlon pursuit. The host Italians defeated Canada in men's curling, while Switzerland did the same in men's ice hockey to put the Canadians on the wrong end of two major upsets in the same day. The United States men's ice hockey team suffered its first loss of the tournament as <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Slovakia at the 2006 Winter Olympics">Slovakia</a> and Russia continue their dominance of the pool.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_10">Day 10</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Day 10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lascelles_Brown" title="Lascelles Brown">Lascelles Brown</a> became the first Jamaican-born competitor to win a medal at the Winter Olympics on February 19, competing on the Canadian 2-man bobsleigh team which finished second in an extremely tight competition. The German pair was only .21 seconds ahead of the Canadians, themselves only .14 ahead of the Swiss team. Finland continued to be unbeaten in men's ice hockey, handing Canada its second loss.</p>
<p>The day also saw the most hyped event of these games, at least in Europe, as the Men's 10 km Cross Country Relay was scheduled. The battle stemmed from the <a href="/wiki/1994_Winter_Olympics" title="1994 Winter Olympics">Lillehammer</a> games 12 years ago in which Italy out-dueled Norway in that very same event. To that extent, many Norwegians wanted to win this event in order to embarrass the Italians on their home turf, but it was not to be as Italy crushed the field winning over Germany by over 15 seconds to take their 5th straight gold in this event. Norway failed to medal for the first time since 1988.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_11">Day 11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Day 11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The final day of curling pool play was February 20; Norway, Sweden, Switzerland, and Canada advanced to the women's semifinals while Finland, Canada, the United States, and Great Britain qualified in the men's competition. Austria took their first team gold medal in ski jumping, while Canada took their second in women's ice hockey to take a 2–1 lead over the United States in all-time Olympic championships.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_12">Day 12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Day 12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Slovakia and Finland both won their final men's ice hockey games on February 21 to win their respective pools with 5–0–0 records. <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fabris" title="Enrico Fabris">Enrico Fabris</a> gave the host nation another gold medal in speed skating by winning the men's 1500 metres.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_13">Day 13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Day 13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 22, the twelfth day of competition, <a href="/wiki/Anja_P%C3%A4rson" title="Anja Pärson">Anja Pärson</a> won her first gold medal in the women's slalom; it was her fifth overall Olympic medal and third of the 2006 Games. <a href="/wiki/Chandra_Crawford" title="Chandra Crawford">Chandra Crawford</a> took a quicker route to the top of the podium, winning the 1.1 kilometre cross-country sprint gold in her Olympic debut. In the men's ice hockey quarterfinals, the previously undefeated Slovakians lost to the Czech Republic while Russia, Finland, and Sweden eliminated Canada, the United States, and Switzerland, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Schoch" title="Philipp Schoch">Philipp Schoch</a> successfully defended his snowboarding giant slalom gold against his brother <a href="/wiki/Simon_Schoch" title="Simon Schoch">Simon</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_14">Day 14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Day 14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sweden took the women's championship in the curling finals held on February 23. <a href="/wiki/Shizuka_Arakawa" title="Shizuka Arakawa">Shizuka Arakawa</a> gave Japan its first gold medal of the Games and first figure skating gold medal, winning the ladies' figure skating competition in part by being able to finish without falling, as <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Cohen" title="Sasha Cohen">Sasha Cohen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irina_Slutskaya" title="Irina Slutskaya">Irina Slutskaya</a> both tumbled. Russia wrested the gold medal in women's team biathlon from two-time defending champions Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_15">Day 15</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Day 15">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>February 24 was the day of the men's curling finals, in which Canada won its first gold medal and the United States won its first medal in the sport as Canada defeated Finland and the United States beat Great Britain for the second time. The figure skating gala was also held, with top placers in all of the events performing exhibitions. Sweden and Finland won their men's ice hockey semifinal games, defeating the Czech Republic and Russia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_16">Day 16</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Day 16">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Austrians swept the men's alpine slalom medals on February 25, led by <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Raich" title="Benjamin Raich">Benjamin Raich</a>. Germany took gold medals in the men's 15 kilometer biathlon and the men's individual bobsleigh. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apolo_Anton_Ohno" title="Apolo Anton Ohno">Apolo Anton Ohno</a> won his second short track speed skating gold medal, with only somewhat less controversy than his first 4 years earlier. South Korea's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jin_Sun-Yu" title="Jin Sun-Yu">Jin Sun-Yu</a> wins her third gold of the Games in the women's 1000 m. Compatriot <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahn_Hyun-Soo" title="Ahn Hyun-Soo">Ahn Hyun-Soo</a> wins his third gold medal of the Games, medaling in every men's short track event and bringing his total number of medals in Turin to four.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Day_17_.28Closing_ceremony.29">Day 17 (Closing ceremony)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Day 17 (Closing ceremony)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The final day of competition and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics_Closing_Ceremony" title="2006 Winter Olympics Closing Ceremony">closing ceremony</a>, were held on February 26. The Swedish men's ice hockey team handed Finland their first loss in the final to take the gold medal. In the closing ceremony, <a href="/wiki/Manuela_Di_Centa" title="Manuela Di Centa">Manuela Di Centa</a>, a seven-time Olympic medalist from Italy and then-member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>, was scheduled to present the medals for the men's 50-kilometre cross-country skiing event. This resulted in her presenting the gold medal to her own brother when <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Di_Centa" title="Giorgio Di Centa">Giorgio Di Centa</a> won the event to take his second gold medal.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_areas">Olympic areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Olympic areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Olympic events were mainly held in Turin, but other events (namely skiing, snowboarding, and the track sports) were held in mountainous outlying villages for obvious reasons.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turin">Turin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Turin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Many venues were located in the Olympic District in central Turin, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oval_Lingotto" title="Oval Lingotto">Oval Lingotto</a> – Speed skating</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Torino_Esposizioni" title="Torino Esposizioni">Torino Esposizioni</a> – Ice hockey</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torino_Palasport_Olimpico" title="Torino Palasport Olimpico">Palasport Olimpico</a> – Ice hockey (final)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico_(Turin)" title="Stadio Olimpico (Turin)">Stadio Olimpico</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics_Opening_Ceremony" title="2006 Winter Olympics Opening Ceremony">Opening</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics_Closing_Ceremony" title="2006 Winter Olympics Closing Ceremony">closing</a> ceremonies</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Torino_Palavela" title="Torino Palavela">Palavela</a> – Figure skating, short-track speed skating</li>
<li>Olympic Village</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_National_Olympic_Committees">Participating National Olympic Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Participating National Olympic Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="1379" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG/300px-2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG/450px-2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG/600px-2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2006_Winter_olympics_team_numbers.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Participating NOCs. Green: 1–9; blue: 10–49; orange: 50–99; red: 100 or more.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A record 80 <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> (NOCs) entered athletes at the 2006 Winter Olympic Games. This was an increase of two from the 78 represented at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002_Olympic_Winter_Games" title="2002 Olympic Winter Games">2002 Olympic Winter Games</a>. The number in parentheses indicates the number of participants that NOC contributed. It was the first appearance for Albania, Ethiopia and Madagascar. It was the only appearance at the Winter Olympics for <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>, coming between their change of name in 2003 and Montenegro's vote for independence in May.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Out of 40,000 applicants, 20,000 volunteers were selected to help the athletes, spectators, and journalists, and to prepare the competition sites. They were selected by the recruiting program <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Noi2006&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Noi2006 (page does not exist)">Noi2006</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Volunteers_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Volunteers-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sixty-five sporting facilities, various infrastructures, sport villages for athletes and media, and transportation infrastructures were constructed for a total of 1.7 billion euros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Construction_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Construction-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the most important sporting facilities that were used:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico_(Turin)" title="Stadio Olimpico (Turin)">Stadio Olimpico (Turin)</a> (formerly known as Stadio Comunale);</li>
<li>Five sports halls (three new, two rearranged): the Palazzo a Vela re-designed by Gae Aulenti (to host short track and ice skating), the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Lingotto" title="Oval Lingotto">Oval Lingotto</a> (speed ice skating), <a href="/wiki/Torino_Esposizioni" title="Torino Esposizioni">Torino Esposizioni</a> (ice hockey), the Ice stadium in corso Tazzoli, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torino_Palasport_Olimpico" title="Torino Palasport Olimpico">Palasport Olimpico</a> designed by Arata Isozaki (ice hockey);</li>
<li>The Olympic arch of Turin;</li>
<li>Olympic villages of Turin, Bardonecchia and Sestriere;</li>
<li>The ice stadium in Pinerolo, re-arranged and enlarged, to host the curling competition;</li>
<li>A new stadium in Torre Pellice (ice hockey);</li>
<li>Twelve new intermediate-level ski lifts in Cesana Torinese, Cesana San Sicario, Sestriere, Bardonecchia, Claviere, Sauze d'Oulx, Pragelato;</li>
<li>The tracks for bobsled, luge, and skeleton in Cesana (the second international track in Italy, along with the one in <a href="/wiki/Cortina_d%27Ampezzo" title="Cortina d'Ampezzo">Cortina d'Ampezzo</a>);</li>
</ul>
<p>The most important transport infrastructure works were:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metrotorino" title="Metrotorino">Turin Metro</a> (<a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9hicule_Automatique_L%C3%A9ger" title="Véhicule Automatique Léger">VAL</a> system), which for the Olympic games connected <a href="/wiki/Collegno" title="Collegno">Collegno</a> to the railway station of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porta_Susa" title="Porta Susa">Porta Susa</a>.</li>
<li>The upgrade of 11 state roads and motorways connecting Turin with other Olympic sites, including the Motorway between Turin and Pinerolo, which was host to the Curling events.</li>
</ul>
<p>In the city, the main developments were the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Palafuksas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Palafuksas (page does not exist)">Palafuksas</a>, a glass building designed by <a href="/wiki/Massimiliano_Fuksas" title="Massimiliano Fuksas">Massimiliano Fuksas</a>, the new Modern Art Gallery and the great project of the "Spina", that will provide urban regeneration over an area of 2 million square meters through the construction of an underground urban railway and the re-utilization of abandoned industrial areas.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Games had issues with costs covering and international attendance. Due to a lack of funding by the Italian Government, Toroc risked dissolution. American skier <a href="/wiki/Bode_Miller" title="Bode Miller">Bode Miller</a> was also a focus of controversy in his home country and Canada, where his actions were not considered in line with the Olympic spirit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Turin_Metro" title="Turin Metro">metro</a> was finally opened to the public on February 4, 2006, after a 45-day delay. It operated on a shorter stretch (<i>XVIII Dicembre</i> (Porta Susa) to <i>Fermi</i> – 11 stations) than originally forecast; it finally reached the main railway station (<i>Porta Nuova</i>) and the rest of the city centre more than one year after the Games, in October 2007. For the duration of the Games, a single ticket (5 euros) covered use of both the metro and other means of public transportation for a whole day. However, during the Games, metro service stopped at 6:00 pm, making it impractical for spectators of evening events. Furthermore, the metro did not reach any of the Olympic venues. On the other hand, the bus service was heavily improved for the Games, although still inadequate at night hours.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doping">Doping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Doping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the games, Italian police raided the Austrian athletes' quarters in search of evidence of blood doping. The raid was conducted due to suspicions over the presence of biathlon coach <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mayer" title="Walter Mayer">Walter Mayer</a>, who had been banned from all Olympic events up to and including the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">Vancouver Olympic Games in 2010</a> due to previous doping convictions. Around the time of the raid Mayer and two Austrian biathletes, Wolfgang Perner and Wolfgang Rottmann, tried to escape and fled back to Austria. Later, the Austrian ski federation president said that the two athletes told him they "may have used illegal methods". Six skiers and four biathletes were also taken for drug screens by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC" title="IOC">IOC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Those substance screens later returned negative results.</p>
<p>On 25 April 2007, six Austrian athletes (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roland_Diethard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roland Diethard (page does not exist)">Roland Diethard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Eder" title="Johannes Eder">Johannes Eder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Perner" title="Wolfgang Perner">Wolfgang Perner</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Pinter" title="Jürgen Pinter">Jürgen Pinter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Rottmann" title="Wolfgang Rottmann">Wolfgang Rottmann</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Tauber&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martin Tauber (page does not exist)">Martin Tauber</a>) were banned for life from the Olympics for their involvement in the doping scandal at the 2006 Turin Olympics, the first time the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC" title="IOC">IOC</a> punished athletes without a positive or missed doping test. The Austrians were found guilty of possessing doping substances and taking part in a conspiracy, based on materials seized by Italian police during the raid on the living quarters. The Austrians also had their competition results from Turin annulled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AustTurin_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-AustTurin-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>List of athletes with doping convictions in these Games:</p>
<ul>
<li>Russian <a href="/wiki/Olga_Medvedtseva" title="Olga Medvedtseva">Olga Medvedtseva</a> was stripped of her silver and other medals in the 15 km biathlon event after testing positive for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carphedon" title="Carphedon">carphedon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>Brazilian bobsled athlete <a href="/wiki/Armando_dos_Santos_(bobsleigh)" title="Armando dos Santos (bobsleigh)">Armando dos Santos</a>, ejected from the Games after a preventive antidoping test came positive (the results were from a test conducted in Brazil).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdS2006_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdS2006-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The IOC has retested nearly 500 doping samples that were collected at the 2006 Turin Games. In 2014, the Estonian Olympic Committee was notified by the IOC that a retested sample from cross-country skier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kristina_%C5%A0migun" title="Kristina Šmigun">Kristina Šmigun</a> had tested positive. On 24 October 2016, the <a href="/wiki/World_Anti-Doping_Agency" title="World Anti-Doping Agency">World Anti-Doping Agency</a> Athletes' Commission stated that Šmigun, who won two gold medals at the Turin Games, faces a <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Arbitration_for_Sport" title="Court of Arbitration for Sport">Court of Arbitration for Sport</a> hearing before the end of October. If Šmigun were to be stripped of her gold medals, Kateřina Neumannová of Czech Republic could be elevated to gold in the <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_15_kilometre_pursuit" title="Cross-country skiing at the 2006 Winter Olympics – Women's 15 kilometre pursuit">7.5 + 7.5 km double pursuit</a> event. Marit Bjørgen of Norway could acquire a seventh gold medal in the <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_10_kilometre_classical" title="Cross-country skiing at the 2006 Winter Olympics – Women's 10 kilometre classical">10 km classical</a> event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ratings_and_attendance">Ratings and attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Ratings and attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this article <b>may not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">You may <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Talk:2006 Winter Olympics">talk page</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_wizard" title="Wikipedia:Article wizard">create a new article</a>, as appropriate.</span> <small><i>(February 2010)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A number of events reported low spectator attendance despite having acceptable ticket sales. Preliminary competition and locally less popular sports failed to attract capacity crowd as expected. Organizers explained this was because blocks of seats were reserved or purchased by sponsors and partners who later did not show up at the events.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Several news organizations reported that many Americans were not as interested in the Olympics as in years past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interest_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Interest-38">[38]</a></sup> It has been suggested that reasons for this lack of interest include the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_delay" title="Broadcast delay">tape delayed</a> coverage, which showed events in prime-time as much as 18 hours later in the Western United States, and also due to the lack of success achieved by big-name American athletes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ratings_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ratings-39">[39]</a></sup> Primetime viewing figures in Canada were also disappointing, especially after the early exit of the Canadian men's hockey team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada_ratings_2_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_ratings_2-40">[40]</a></sup> though overall viewing figures were up from 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canada_ratings_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_ratings-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Legacy">Olympic Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Olympic Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oval2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oval2009.jpg/220px-Oval2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oval2009.jpg/330px-Oval2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Oval2009.jpg/440px-Oval2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oval2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Torino's Olympic Oval hosting the 2009 European Athletics Indoor</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Olympics represented an opportunity to revamp the city's look and change its traditional image as an industrial city by showing the world its hidden side of vibrant cultural life and stunning architectures. Thanks to the olympic exposure and state of the art venues, Turin has become one of Italy's primary tourist destinations and has been established as an important sport center in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2006, TOP (<a href="/wiki/Torino_Olympic_Park" title="Torino Olympic Park">Torino Olympic Park</a>) had been the agency in charge of managing the Olympic facilities.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_measures">Security measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Winter_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Security measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As with every Olympics since the <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> and increasingly since the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">Salt Lake 2002 Winter Olympics</a>, there was heavy security due to fears of terrorism.</p>
<p>The organizers further increased security measures<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> in connection with the <a href="/wiki/Jyllands-Posten_Muhammad_cartoons_controversy" title="Jyllands-Posten Muhammad cartoons controversy">Jyllands-Posten Muhammad cartoons controversy</a> and insisted that the Olympic Games were going to be safe, which they were; the Olympics concluded without a major breach of security occurring.</p>
